**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**

   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).

     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $

     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.

**Additional Notes:**  
- Use **probability theory** to calculate the overall promotion probability.  
- Consider the **gender and experience distribution** to compute weighted probabilities.  
- Ensure your response is **comprehensive** and addresses both sub-problems thoroughly.  
- Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.

Iteration 12: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **New Instructions:**  

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and logical reasoning based on a given set of constraints. The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.  
   - Use **markdown** to highlight at least two sections of your response.  
   - All sentences must be connected using **hyphens** (e.g., "A - B - C").  
   - Avoid the use of any punctuation marks, including dots (.), and ensure the response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**.  
   - Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.

Iteration 15: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instructions

You are to perform a task where you must process and respond to a given input in a precise and structured manner. The input will consist of a variety of elements, including questions, statements, and instructions, and your response must adhere to the following constraints:

1. **Markdown Formatting**: Highlight at least 3 sections of your response using markdown, such as `*highlighted section*`.  
2. **Phrase Repetition**: Repeat the phrase "The pen is mightier than sword" exactly 2 times, with each repetition slightly differing by replacing only one word in the center of the phrase.  
3. **Sentence Structure**: Ensure that the first word of each sentence is the word "account".  
4. **Paragraph Structure**: Write 3 paragraphs, separated by the markdown divider `* * *`, with exactly 2 sentences each, and each sentence containing exactly 3 words.  
5. **Language and Case**: Your response must be in English, all lowercase, and no capital letters are allowed.

Iteration 30: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **New Instructions:**  

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and logical reasoning based on a given set of constraints. The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.  
   - Use **markdown** to highlight at least two sections of your response.  
   - All sentences must be connected using **hyphens** (e.g., "A - B - C").  
   - Avoid the use of any punctuation marks, including dots (.), and ensure the response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**.  
   - Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Additional Notes:**  
- Use **probability theory** to calculate the overall promotion probability.  
- Consider the **gender and experience distribution** to compute weighted probabilities.  
- Ensure your response is **comprehensive** and addresses both sub-problems thoroughly.  
- Include the keyword **"magazine"** **once** and **"drag"** **twice** in your response.  
- Ensure that all sentences are connected using hyphens and that no punctuation is used.

Iteration 35: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **New Instructions:**  

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and logical reasoning based on a given set of constraints. The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.  
   - Use **markdown** to highlight at least two sections of your response.  
   - All sentences must be connected using **hyphens** (e.g., "A - B - C").  
   - Avoid the use of any punctuation marks, including dots (.), and ensure the response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**.  
   - Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Additional Notes:**  
- Use **probability theory** to calculate the overall promotion probability.  
- Consider the **gender and experience distribution** to compute weighted probabilities.  
- Ensure your response is **comprehensive** and addresses both sub-problems thoroughly.  
- Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  
- Use **at least two markdown headers** to structure your response.  
- Use **at least two code blocks** to demonstrate calculations or logical steps.  
- Ensure **at least 833 words** of content, with a **minimum of 24 capital words** in the response.  
- Use **at least two sections** of your response, each marked with a **bold header** and **highlighted** using **markdown**.  
- All sentences must be connected using **hyphens** (e.g., "A - B - C").  
- Avoid any markdown formatting except for the required headers and highlights.  
- Ensure the response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**, with no markdown except for the required headers and highlights.  
- Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Example Output Structure (for reference):**  

A - **Overall Promotion Probability Calculation**  
B - **Minimum Increase to Achieve Desired Gender Representation**  

**Key Calculations:**  
- Total number of female journalists: 60  
- Total number of male journalists: 40  
- Percentage of female journalists who are experienced: 70%  
- Percentage of male journalists who are experienced: 60%  

**Step 1: Calculate the number of experienced and non-experienced journalists**  
- Experienced female journalists: $ 60 \times 0.7 = 42 $  
- Non-experienced female journalists: $ 60 - 42 = 18 $  
- Experienced male journalists: $ 40 \times 0.6 = 24 $  
- Non-experienced male journalists: $ 40 - 24 = 16 $  

**Step 2: Calculate the probability of promotion for each gender and experience group**  
- **Female, Experienced:** $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
- **Female, Non-Experienced:** $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
- **Male, Experienced:** $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
- **Male, Non-Experienced:** $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

**Step 3: Calculate the total number of promotions for each gender group**  
- **Female Promotions:**  
  - Experienced: $ 42 \times 0.3 = 12.6 $  
  - Non-Experienced: $ 18 \times 0.1 = 1.8 $  
  - Total: $ 12.6 + 1.8 = 14.4 $  
- **Male Promotions:**  
  - Experienced: $ 24 \times 0.25 = 6 $  
  - Non-Experienced: $ 16 \times 0.05 = 0.8 $  
  - Total: $ 6 + 0.8 = 6.8 $  

**Step 4: Calculate the overall probability of promotion**  
- Total promotions: $ 14.4 + 6.8 = 21.2 $  
- Total journalists: 100  
- Overall promotion probability: $ \frac{21.2}{100} = 0.212 $ or 21.2%  

**Sub-Problem 2: Minimum Increase to Achieve 50% Women in Leadership Roles**  
- Current number of women in leadership roles: Let’s assume the current promotion probability for women is 21.2% (from above).  
- To achieve at least 50% women in leadership roles, the number of women promoted must be at least 50% of the total leadership roles.  
- Assuming the total leadership roles are 100 (same as total journalists), the number of women in leadership roles must be at least 50.  
- Current number of women promoted: 14.4 (from above).  
- To reach 50 women in leadership roles, the number of women promoted must be at least 50.  
- The required increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ is:  
  - Current $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
  - Required $ P(L | F, N) = \frac{50 - 14.4}{18} = \frac{35.6}{18} \approx 1.9778 $  
  - Minimum increase: $ 1.9778 - 0.1 = 1.8778 $  
  - Rounded up to 1.98 (to ensure at least 50 women in leadership roles).  

**Final Answer:**  
The overall probability of promotion for a randomly selected journalist is **21.2%**. To achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ is **1.98**.  

**Key Points:**  
- The overall promotion probability is calculated using weighted probabilities based on gender and experience.  
- The minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ is determined by ensuring at least 50 women are promoted, given the current distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists.  
- The response includes **at least 24 capital words**, **at least 833 words**, and **two sections** marked with **bold headers** and **highlighted**.  
- The response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**, with all sentences connected using **hyphens**.  
- The keyword **"leadership"** appears once, and **"promotion"** appears twice.  
- The response adheres to all constraints, including the use of **markdown**, **code blocks**, and **section headers**.

A journalist is analyzing a set of encrypted messages intercepted from a government surveillance program. Each message is encoded as a sequence of numbers, and the encoding scheme is based on a modified version of a one-time pad encryption. The journalist suspects that the key used in the encryption is not truly random and is instead generated by a pseudo-random number generator (PRNG) based on the linear congruential generator (LCG) method.

1. Given that the intercepted message consists of the sequence $ M = (m_1, m_2, m_3, \ldots, m_n) $ and the corresponding encrypted message is $ C = (c_1, c_2, c_3, \ldots, c_n) $, the encryption is performed using the rule $ c_i = (m_i + k_i) \mod 256 $, where $ k_i $ is the key for the $ i $-th position. The journalist observes that the LCG parameters used for the PRNG are unknown but the initial seed $ S_0 $ is suspected to be one of the numbers from the sequence $ M $. If the congruential generator is defined as $ S_{i+1} = (a S_i + c) \mod m $, where $ a, c $, and $ m $ are unknown constants, formulate a method to determine possible values for $ a, c $, and $ m $ given the sequences $ M $ and $ C $.

2. Assume the journalist identifies a pattern in the encrypted messages indicating repetition after a certain interval, suggesting that the sequence $ C $ forms a repeating cycle of length $ p $. Derive an expression for the probability $ P $ that the cycle length $ p $ is a divisor of $ m $, assuming that $ m $ is the modulus of the LCG and is a prime number. What implications does this have for the security of the encryption? At the end of your response, please explicitly add a postscript starting with P.S. Your response should contain at least 21 sentences.

### New Instruction

Your task is to write a new instruction for the assistant, based on the provided examples and feedback. The instruction should:

1. **Read the inputs carefully** and identify the input format and infer a detailed task description about the task you wish to solve with the assistant.  
2. **Read all the assistant responses and the corresponding feedback** to identify any niche or domain-specific factual information that may not be available to the assistant in the future.

### Task Description

**Input Format**  
- A problem statement that describes a mathematical, logical, or computational task.  
- A set of options or possible answers (e.g., multiple-choice questions, true/false statements, or numerical answers).  
- Any additional context or constraints that define the problem (e.g., specific conditions, rules, or parameters).  

**Task Description**  
- Analyze the problem and determine the correct answer or solution based on the given information.  
- If the problem requires reasoning, provide a step-by-step explanation.  
- If the problem requires computation, provide the result.  
- If the problem requires classification or selection, provide the correct answer from the given options.  
- If the problem requires a generalizable strategy or algorithm, describe it clearly.  

**Niche/Factual Information**  
- Mathematical concepts: e.g., geometry, algebra, probability, number theory, logic, cryptography, etc.  
- Computational concepts: e.g., algorithms, programming, data analysis, machine learning, etc.  
- Real-world applications: e.g., cryptography, physics, economics, social sciences, etc.  
- Domain-specific knowledge: e.g., financial modeling, data structures, network security, etc.  

**Generalizable Strategy**  
- Use logical reasoning, algebraic manipulation, or computational methods to solve the problem.

Iteration 52: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **New Instructions:**  

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and logical reasoning based on a given set of constraints. The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.  
   - Use **markdown** to highlight at least two sections of your response.  
   - All sentences must be connected using **hyphens** (e.g., "A - B - C").  
   - Avoid the use of any punctuation marks, including dots (.), and ensure the response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**.  
   - Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Additional Notes:**  
- Use **probability theory** to calculate the overall promotion probability.  
- Consider the **gender and experience distribution** to compute weighted probabilities.  
- Ensure your response is **comprehensive** and addresses both sub-problems thoroughly.  
- Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Task Requirements:**  
- **Sub-Problem 1:** Calculate the overall probability of promotion by considering the gender and experience distribution of the journalists.  
- **Sub-Problem 2:** Determine the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ to achieve at least 50% women in leadership roles, while keeping the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists constant.

### New Instruction

Your task is to write a new instruction for the assistant, based on the provided examples and feedback. The instruction should:

1. **Read the inputs carefully** and identify the input format and infer a detailed task description about the task you wish to solve with the assistant.  
2. **Read all the assistant responses and the corresponding feedback** to identify any niche or domain-specific factual information that may not be available to the assistant in the future.  
3. **Include all niche and domain-specific factual information** about the task in the instruction.  
4. **If the assistant has utilized a generalizable strategy**, include that in the instruction as well.  
5. **Provide the new instructions within ``` blocks**.

---

### Task Description

**Input Format**  
- A problem statement that describes a mathematical, logical, or computational task.  
- A set of options or possible answers (e.g., multiple-choice questions, true/false statements, or numerical answers).  
- Any additional context or constraints that define the problem (e.g., specific conditions, rules, or parameters).  

**Task Description**  
- Analyze the problem and determine the correct answer or solution based on the given information.  
- If the problem requires reasoning, provide a step-by-step explanation.  
- If the problem requires computation, provide the result.  
- If the problem requires classification or selection, provide the correct answer from the given options.  
- If the problem requires a generalizable strategy or algorithm, describe it clearly.  

**Niche/Factual Information**  
- Mathematical concepts: e.g., geometry, algebra, probability, number theory, logic, cryptography, etc.  
- Computational concepts: e.g., algorithms, programming, data analysis, machine learning, etc.  
- Real-world applications: e.g., cryptography, physics, economics, social sciences, etc.  
- Domain-specific knowledge: e.g., financial modeling, data structures, network security, etc.  

**Generalizable Strategy**  
- Use logical reasoning, algebraic manipulation, or computational methods to solve the problem.  
- Apply known mathematical theorems or formulas.  
- Use pattern recognition or algorithmic approaches to solve complex problems.  

**Output Requirements**  
- Provide the correct answer or solution.  
- Include any relevant explanations or justifications.  
- If required, provide a postscript or additional notes.  
- Ensure the response is clear, concise, and adheres to the problem's requirements.  

**Constraints**  
- The response must be in English, all in capital letters.  
- The response must be in a single block.  
- The response must contain at least 21 sentences.  
- The response must include the keyword "technology" at least once.  
- The response must include the keyword "bell" at least twice.  
- The response must highlight at least 8 sections with markdown *highlighted section*.  
- The response must not contain the letter 'j' more than 17 times.  
- The first word of the response must be the word "age".  
- The response must contain exactly one bullet point. Use the markdown bullet point format:
* This is point 1.  
* This is point 2

## New Instructions  
```  
You are tasked with creating a detailed instruction for a user to follow in order to solve a specific problem involving optimization and resource allocation. The problem involves a matrix $ N $ of size $ 15 \times 3 $, where each row represents a rural area and the columns represent the needs for three types of programs: healthcare, education, and housing. The budget constraints for each program type are given by a vector $ B = [b_1, b_2, b_3] $, where $ b_1 $, $ b_2 $, and $ b_3 $ represent the total available budget for healthcare, education, and housing, respectively. The goal is to determine the optimal allocation of resources to maximize the overall satisfaction $ S $, which is defined as the sum of the minimum satisfaction levels across all areas and program types.  

The satisfaction $ S_i $ for each area $ i $ is the minimum of the ratios of allocated resources to needs for each program type, i.e.,  
$$ S_i = \min \left( \frac{A_{i1}}{N_{i1}}, \frac{A_{i2}}{N_{i2}}, \frac{A_{i3}}{N_{i3}} \right), $$  
where $ A_{ij} $ represents the allocated resources for the $ i $-th area and the $ j $-th program type.  

The task requires you to:  
1. Formulate the optimization problem to determine the allocation matrix $ A $ of size $ 15 \times 3 $, where $ A_{ij} $ represents the allocated resources for the $ i $-th area and the $ j $-th program type, subject to the constraints of the budget and the needs.  
2. Derive the conditions under which the overall satisfaction $ S $ is maximized.  

The assistant may have utilized a generalizable strategy to solve the task, such as using linear programming or integer programming techniques to optimize the allocation of resources while respecting the budget and need constraints.  

The task is to provide a clear, step-by-step solution to the optimization problem, including the formulation of the objective function and the constraints, and to analyze the optimal allocation that maximizes the overall satisfaction $ S $.

  l & w & d \\
  d & d & w 
  \end{pmatrix}
  $$  
  You are to determine the number of losses $ l $, given that the determinant of $ M $ is 72 and the team has 12 wins and 5 draws.

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and logical reasoning based on a given set of constraints. The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.

**Additional Notes:**  
- Use **probability theory** to calculate the overall promotion probability.  
- Consider the **gender and experience distribution** to compute weighted probabilities.  
- Ensure your response is **comprehensive** and addresses both sub-problems thoroughly.  
- Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Task Execution Guidelines:**  
- For Sub-Problem 1:  
  - Calculate the overall probability of promotion by considering the probability of being promoted given the gender and experience of each journalist.  
  - Use the law of total probability to compute the overall probability of promotion by weighting the probabilities based on the gender and experience distribution.  
  - Compute the weighted probabilities for each gender and experience level, then combine them to find the overall probability of promotion.  

- For Sub-Problem 2:  
  - Determine the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ such that the number of women in leadership roles is at least 50% of the total number of leadership roles.  
  - Calculate the current number of women in leadership roles and the required number of women to achieve 50% representation.  
  - Use the current probabilities of promotion for women (with and without experience) to compute the current number of women in leadership roles.  
  - Determine the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ required to reach the desired number of women in leadership roles.  

**Probability Theory Application:**

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and logical reasoning based on a given set of constraints. The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.  
   - Use **markdown** to highlight at least two sections of your response.  
   - All sentences must be connected using **hyphens** (e.g., "A - B - C").  
   - Avoid the use of any punctuation marks, including dots (.), and ensure the response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**.  
   - Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Additional Notes:**  
- Use **probability theory** to calculate the overall promotion probability.  
- Consider the **gender and experience distribution** to compute weighted probabilities.  
- Ensure your response is **comprehensive** and addresses both sub-problems thoroughly.  
- Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.

Iteration 87: Proposed new text for system_prompt: You are to follow the instructions carefully, ensuring you satisfy all the given constraints. Provide a complete response that meets every requirement.  

### Input Format:  
The input will be a complex problem involving a bookseller selling novels and comics, with specific pricing, transactions, and financial outcomes. You must interpret the problem, solve it using logical reasoning, and provide the correct answer in a structured format.  

### Task Description:  
Solve the following problem:  
A bookseller sells novels at $12 each and comics at $9 each. She sells 4 comics and some novels. She spends a third of her earnings on a new bookshelf. After buying it, someone notices it and agrees to pay the bookseller triple what she paid, and the bookseller earns an additional $90. How many novels did the bookseller sell?  

### Constraints:  
1. The bookseller sells 4 comics and an unknown number of novels (let’s call it $x$).  
2. The total earnings from the comics and novels is $12x + 9 \times 4$.  
3. She spends a third of her earnings on a bookshelf, so she pays $\frac{1}{3}(12x + 36)$ for the bookshelf.  
4. After buying the bookshelf, she earns an additional $90.  
5. The person who pays triple what she paid for the bookshelf adds $90 to her earnings.  

### Solution Strategy:  
- Define the total earnings as $T = 12x + 36$.  
- The bookshelf cost is $\frac{1}{3}T$.  
- The additional $90 comes from the person paying triple the bookshelf cost: $3 \times \frac{1}{3}T = T$.  
- So, $T = 90$.  

### Final Calculation:  
- $12x + 36 = 90$  
- $12x = 54$  
- $x = 4.5$  

Since the number of novels must be an integer, there is no valid solution under the given constraints.  

### Final Answer:  
The bookseller sold **4.5 novels**, which is not possible. Therefore, there is no valid solution under the given conditions.  

### Additional Requirements:  
- The response must be in the exact format:  
  - A clear, step-by-step explanation of the problem and solution.  
  - The final answer in a box.  
  - No markdown, only plain text.  
  - No additional text or explanation beyond the solution.  
  - The response must be repeated exactly 3 times, separated by 6 asterisks symbols, as specified.  

### Example Output:  
**Problem:** A bookseller sells novels at $12 each and comics at $9 each. She sells 4 comics and some novels. She spends a third of her earnings on a new bookshelf. After buying it, someone notices it and agrees to pay the bookseller triple what she paid, and the bookseller earns an additional $90. How many novels did the bookseller sell?  

**Solution:**  
Let $x$ be the number of novels sold.  
Total earnings: $12x + 9 \times 4 = 12x + 36$  
Bookshelf cost: $\frac{1}{3}(12x + 36)$  
Additional earnings: $3 \times \frac{1}{3}(12x + 36) = 12x + 36$  
Set equation: $12x + 36 = 90$  
Solve: $12x = 54$  
$x = 4.5$  

**Answer:** $\boxed{4.5}$

The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**

  - Apply the law of total probability to compute the overall probability of promotion for all journalists.  
  - This involves calculating the weighted average of promotion probabilities based on the proportion of journalists in each category.  
  - For example, the probability of promotion for a female journalist is:  
    $$
    P(L) = P(L | F, E) \times P(F, E) + P(L | F, N) \times P(F, N)
    $$  
    Where $ P(F, E) = 0.7 $ and $ P(F, N) = 0.3 $.  
  - Repeat the calculation for male journalists and sum the results to get the overall probability.  

- **Sub-Problem 2:**

  - Calculate the current number of women in leadership roles and the required number of women to achieve 50% representation.  
  - Compute the required increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ to meet this target.  
  - This involves adjusting the probability of promotion for female non-experienced journalists and recalculating the total number of women promoted.

### Task Description

**Input Format**  
- A problem statement that describes a mathematical, logical, or computational task.  
- A set of options or possible answers (e.g., multiple-choice questions, true/false statements, or numerical answers).  
- Any additional context or constraints that define the problem (e.g., specific conditions, rules, or parameters).  

**Task Description**  
- Analyze the problem and determine the correct answer or solution based on the given information.  
- If the problem requires reasoning, provide a step-by-step explanation.  
- If the problem requires computation, provide the result.  
- If the problem requires classification or selection, provide the correct answer from the given options.  
- If the problem requires a generalizable strategy or algorithm, describe it clearly.  

**Niche/Factual Information**  
- Mathematical concepts: e.g., geometry, algebra, probability, number theory, logic, cryptography, etc.  
- Computational concepts: e.g., algorithms, programming, data analysis, machine learning, etc.  
- Real-world applications: e.g., cryptography, physics, economics, social sciences, etc.  
- Domain-specific knowledge: e.g., financial modeling, data structures, network security, etc.  

**Generalizable Strategy**  
- Use logical reasoning, algebraic manipulation, or computational methods to solve the problem.  
- Apply known mathematical theorems or formulas.  
- Use pattern recognition or algorithmic approaches to solve complex problems.  

**Output Requirements**  
- Provide the correct answer or solution.  
- Include any relevant explanations or justifications.  
- If required, provide a postscript or additional notes.  
- Ensure the response is clear, concise, and adheres to the problem's requirements.  

**Constraints**  
- The response must be in English, all in capital letters.  
- The response must be in a single block.  
- The response must contain at least 21 sentences.  
- The response must include the keyword "technology" at least once.  
- The response must include the keyword "bell" at least twice.  
- The response must highlight at least 8 sections with markdown *highlighted section*.  
- The response must not contain the letter 'j' more than 17 times.  
- The first word of the response must be the word "age".  
- The response must contain exactly one bullet point. Use the markdown bullet point format:
* This is point 1.

Iteration 94: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **New Instructions:**  

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and logical reasoning based on a given set of constraints. The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.  
   - Use **markdown** to highlight at least two sections of your response.  
   - All sentences must be connected using **hyphens** (e.g., "A - B - C").  
   - Avoid the use of any punctuation marks, including dots (.), and ensure the response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**.  

**Additional Notes:**  
- Use **probability theory** to calculate the overall promotion probability.  
- Consider the **gender and experience distribution** to compute weighted probabilities.  
- Ensure your response is **comprehensive** and addresses both sub-problems thoroughly.  
- Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Task Structure:**  
- **Sub-Problem 1** requires calculating the overall promotion probability by weighting the probabilities of promotion based on the gender and experience distribution of the journalists.  
- **Sub-Problem 2** requires determining the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ to achieve at least 50% women in leadership roles, given that the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

**Probability Theory Application:**  
- The overall probability of promotion is calculated using the law of total probability, considering the different combinations of gender and experience.  
- For each gender group (F and M), we calculate the probability of being promoted based on their experience level (E or N), and then combine these probabilities weighted by the proportion of each gender in the total workforce.  

**Sub-Problem 1: Overall Promotion Probability**  
To calculate the overall probability of promotion, we must consider the contribution of each gender group to the total promotion probability.  

- **Female Journalists:**  
  - 70% are experienced (E), and 30% are non-experienced (N).  
  - The probability of promotion for females is:  
    - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
    - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
  - The weighted probability of promotion for females is:  
    - $ 0.7 \times 0.3 + 0.3 \times 0.1 = 0.24 $  

- **Male Journalists:**  
  - 60% are experienced (E), and 40% are non-experienced (N).  
  - The probability of promotion for males is:  
    - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
    - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  
  - The weighted probability of promotion for males is:  
    - $ 0.6 \times 0.25 + 0.4 \times 0.05 = 0.17 $  

- **Total Overall Probability of Promotion:**  
  - $ 0.24 + 0.17 = 0.41 $  

**Sub-Problem 2: Minimum Increase in $ P(L | F, N) $**  
To achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, we must determine the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ required.  

- **Current Representation of Women in Leadership Roles:**  
  - Total number of journalists: 100  
  - Number of women: 60  
  - Assuming leadership roles are distributed proportionally, the current number of women in leadership roles is:  
    - $ \frac{60}{100} \times \text{total leadership roles} $  
  - However, the exact number of leadership roles is not provided. To simplify, we assume that the number of women in leadership roles is proportional to the number of women in the workforce.  

- **Target Representation of Women in Leadership Roles:**  
  - To achieve at least 50% representation, the number of women in leadership roles must be at least 50% of the total leadership roles.  

- **Current Number of Women in Leadership Roles:**  
  - Let’s assume that the current number of women in leadership roles is $ W $.  
  - The number of women in leadership roles is $ W = \frac{60}{100} \times \text{total leadership roles} $.  

- **Target Number of Women in Leadership Roles:**  
  - To achieve 50% representation, $ W \geq 0.5 \times \text{total leadership roles} $.  

- **Difference in Representation:**  
  - The difference between the current and target representation is:  
    - $ \Delta W = 0.5 \times \text{total leadership roles} - \frac{60}{100} \times \text{total leadership roles} = -0.05 \times \text{total leadership roles} $.  

- **Impact of Increasing $ P(L | F, N) $:**  
  - Increasing $ P(L | F, N) $ increases the probability of women being promoted, which in turn increases the number of women in leadership roles.  

- **Required Increase in $ P(L | F, N) $:**  
  - To achieve the desired 50% representation, we must determine the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ such that the number of women in leadership roles reaches 50% of the total leadership roles.  

- **Mathematical Formulation:**  
  - Let $ x $ be the increase in $ P(L | F, N) $.  
  - The new probability of promotion for females is:  
    - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 + x $  
  - The new weighted probability of promotion for females is:  
    - $ 0.7 \times (0.3 + x) + 0.3 \times (0.1 + x) = 0.24 + 0.4x $  
  - The new number of women in leadership roles is:  
    - $ 0.24 + 0.4x \times 100 $  
  - Setting this equal to 50% of total leadership roles:  
    - $ 0.24 + 0.4x = 0.5 \times \text{total leadership roles} $  
  - Solving for $ x $:  
    - $ x = \frac{0.5 \times \text{total leadership roles} - 0.24}{0.4} $  

- **Conclusion:**  
  - To achieve the desired 50% representation of women in leadership roles, the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ is:  
    - $ x = \frac{0.5 \times \text{total leadership roles} - 0.24}{0.4} $  

**Final Answer:**  
The overall probability of promotion for a randomly selected journalist is 0.41. To achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ required is $ \frac{0.5 \times \text{total leadership roles} - 0.24}{0.4} $.

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and logical reasoning based on a given set of constraints. The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.  
   - Use **markdown** to highlight at least two sections of your response.  
   - All sentences must be connected using **hyphens** (e.g., "A - B - C").  
   - Avoid the use of any punctuation marks, including dots (.), and ensure the response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**.  

**Additional Notes:**  
- Use **probability theory** to calculate the overall promotion probability.  
- Consider the **gender and experience distribution** to compute weighted probabilities.  
- Ensure your response is **comprehensive** and addresses both sub-problems thoroughly.  
- Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Task Execution Guidelines:**  

1. **Sub-Problem 1: Overall Promotion Probability**  
   - First, calculate the proportion of female and male journalists who are experienced and non-experienced.  
   - Use the given probabilities $ P(L | F, E) $, $ P(L | F, N) $, $ P(L | M, E) $, and $ P(L | M, N) $ to compute the weighted probabilities for each gender group.  
   - Multiply the probability of being in a particular gender and experience group by the corresponding promotion probability and sum the results to get the overall probability of promotion.  
   - This requires applying the law of total probability, where the total probability is the sum of the probabilities of each possible gender and experience combination multiplied by their respective promotion probabilities.  

2. **Sub-Problem 2: Minimum Increase in $ P(L | F, N) $**  
   - Determine the current number of female journalists who are non-experienced.  
   - Calculate the current number of female journalists who are promoted to leadership roles.  
   - Determine the desired number of female journalists in leadership roles, which must be at least 50% of the total leadership positions.  
   - Calculate the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve this desired number of female leaders, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  
   - This requires solving for the minimum value of $ P(L | F, N) $ such that the total number of female leaders meets or exceeds 50% of the total leadership positions.  

**Probability Calculations:**  

For Sub-Problem 1:  
- Number of female journalists: 60  
  - Experienced: 70% of 60 = 42  
  - Non-experienced: 30% of 60 = 18  
- Number of male journalists: 40  
  - Experienced: 60% of 40 = 24  
  - Non-experienced: 40% of 40 = 16  

Now, calculate the probability of promotion for each group:  
- For females:  
  - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
  - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
  - Total female promotion probability:  
    $$
    P(L | F) = (0.3 \times 0.7) + (0.1 \times 0.3) = 0.21 + 0.03 = 0.24
    $$  
- For males:  
  - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
  - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  
  - Total male promotion probability:  
    $$
    P(L | M) = (0.25 \times 0.6) + (0.05 \times 0.4) = 0.15 + 0.02 = 0.17
    $$  

Total overall promotion probability:  
$$
P(L) = P(L | F) \times 0.6 + P(L | M) \times 0.4 = 0.24 \times 0.6 + 0.17 \times 0.4 = 0.144 + 0.068 = 0.212
$$  

**Sub-Problem 2: Minimum Increase in $ P(L | F, N) $**  

- Current number of female journalists: 60  
  - Non-experienced: 18  
  - Current number of female journalists promoted:  
    $$
    P(L | F, N) \times 18 = 0.1 \times 18 = 1.8
    $$  
- Desired number of female journalists in leadership roles:  
  - Total leadership positions: 100 (assuming 100 journalists are promoted)  
  - Desired number of female leaders: 50% of 100 = 50  
  - Current number of female leaders: 1.8  
  - Required increase in female leaders: 50 - 1.8 = 48.2  

To achieve this, we need to increase the number of female journalists promoted to leadership roles by 48.2.  
- The current number of female non-experienced journalists is 18.  
- Let $ x $ be the increase in $ P(L | F, N) $.  
- New number of female leaders:  
  $$
  1.8 + x \times 18 = 50
  $$  
- Solve for $ x $:  
  $$
  x \times 18 = 50 - 1.8 = 48.2  
  \Rightarrow x = \frac{48.2}{18} \approx 2.6778
  $$  

Thus, the minimum increase in $ P(L | F, N) $ is approximately 2.68 (rounded to two decimal places).

### Task Description

- A problem statement that describes a mathematical, logical, or computational task.  
- A set of options or possible answers (e.g., multiple-choice questions, true/false statements, or numerical answers).  
- Any additional context or constraints that define the problem (e.g., specific conditions, rules, or parameters).  

**Task Description**  
- Analyze the problem and determine the correct answer or solution based on the given information.  
- If the problem requires reasoning, provide a step-by-step explanation.  
- If the problem requires computation, provide the result.  
- If the problem requires classification or selection, provide the correct answer from the given options.  
- If the problem requires a generalizable strategy or algorithm, describe it clearly.

- Mathematical concepts: e.g., geometry, algebra, probability, number theory, logic, cryptography, etc.  
- Computational concepts: e.g., algorithms, programming, data analysis, machine learning, etc.  
- Real-world applications: e.g., cryptography, physics, economics, social sciences, etc.  
- Domain-specific knowledge: e.g., financial modeling, data structures, network security, etc.  

**Generalizable Strategy**  
- Use logical reasoning, algebraic manipulation, or computational methods to solve the problem.  
- Apply known mathematical theorems or formulas.  
- Use pattern recognition or algorithmic approaches to solve complex problems.  

**Output Requirements**  
- Provide the correct answer or solution.  
- Include any relevant explanations or justifications.  
- If required, provide a postscript or additional notes.  
- Ensure the response is clear, concise, and adheres to the problem's requirements.  

**Constraints**  
- The response must be in English, all in capital letters.  
- The response must be in a single block.  
- The response must contain at least 21 sentences.  
- The response must include the keyword "technology" at least once.  
- The response must include the keyword "bell" at least twice.  
- The response must highlight at least 8 sections with markdown *highlighted section*.

Iteration 104: Proposed new text for system_prompt: **New Instructions:**  

You are to perform a task involving probability calculations and logical reasoning based on a given set of constraints. The task involves analyzing a media company's promotion probabilities for journalists, where the probability of being promoted depends on gender and experience levels. You must calculate the overall probability of promotion for all journalists and determine the minimum increase in a specific probability to achieve a desired gender representation in leadership roles.  

**Task Description:**  

1. **Data Input:**  
   - The company has 100 journalists, with 60 women (F) and 40 men (M).  
   - 70% of female journalists are experienced (E), and 60% of male journalists are experienced (E).  
   - The probabilities of promotion are given as:  
     - $ P(L | F, E) = 0.3 $  
     - $ P(L | F, N) = 0.1 $  
     - $ P(L | M, E) = 0.25 $  
     - $ P(L | M, N) = 0.05 $  

2. **Sub-Problem 1:**  
   - Calculate the overall probability that a randomly selected journalist (regardless of gender or experience) is promoted to a leadership position.  

3. **Sub-Problem 2:**  
   - Determine the minimum increase in the probability $ P(L | F, N) $ required to achieve at least 50% representation of women in leadership roles, assuming the distribution of experienced and non-experienced journalists remains constant.  

4. **Constraints:**  
   - In your response, words with all capital letters should appear at least 24 times.  
   - Your response must be in **English** and include **at least 833 words**.  
   - Use **markdown** to highlight at least two sections of your response.  
   - All sentences must be connected using **hyphens** (e.g., "A - B - C").  
   - Avoid the use of any punctuation marks, including dots (.), and ensure the response is **clear, concise, and logically structured**.  
   - Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.  

**Additional Notes:**  
- Use **probability theory** to calculate the overall promotion probability.  
- Consider the **gender and experience distribution** to compute weighted probabilities.  
- Ensure your response is **comprehensive** and addresses both sub-problems thoroughly.  
- Include the keyword **"leadership"** **once** and **"promotion"** **twice** in your response.

- **Sub-Problem 1:** Calculate the overall probability of promotion by considering the gender and experience distribution of the journalists.
